< Review>
I live this place. What a spot if beauty tucked into the industrial part of Santa Rosa. I've been there for church services, workshops, mixers & there wonderful Friday night Swing Dances. It is one if the few places where young people can go to dance in a safe, supportive atmosphere. What a treasure that us in today's world. Most recently I've gotten involved with the Wedding Expo,  Dave, who owns Ellington & produces the Expo is an extraordinary man, I've been blessed to meet. I'll be dancing on Friday's, now that my son isn't there telling me I can't come, it's his space....lol<//Review>

<Review>I have been coming to this location for 4 years now and have never been let down by the excellent customer service of the owner and the employees. The food is not winning any awards or anything, but it's just meant to be a convenient, fast meal that's a tad healthier than your average burger or other fast food. I especially love Flame Broiler's choice of sauces, they're particularly good when mixed together (The "Magic" Sauce and the standard red "Hot" sauce). Overall I greatly enjoy the food, especially the beef. My only real complaint is that the drink lids are ridiculously hard to fit onto the cups without making a mess. He seemed more like a friend who was excited about riding than a salesman, and I appreciated that. He gave me his contact information and said I could text him with any more questions. This made me want to drive the 350 miles to his dealership. I went down the next weekend and found the dealership bigger than I thought it was. A clean layout and lots of friendly staff. <Pics>None< /Pics>< Review>
Didn't take long to feel like family at this place. Rich Sesma is a great Representative of Pasadena Yamaha--I would say "Salesman" because that's technically what he functions as--but, he doesn't operate that way. I stumbled by this place on accident late one night, then I came in the next day.

It was freaking 90+ degrees the day I came and they offered water AND bottles of Black Tea. Plus they have couches you can chill on. I was able to take my gear off and relax,

Rich greeted me as I came in and we started talking about bikes and his experiences riding, and even other stories about his life. It was a personable experience I enjoyed. I told him I was looking for a used 2019 R3 and he gave me straightforward information about that bike. Then he showed me this used 2018 Ninja 400 the shop recently acquired that wasn't even on the floor yet because it needed cosmetic repairs. The thing is, we didn't even go back to look at it just so he could sell it to me, he just told me how blown away he was how crazy modified it was; the original owner modified nearly every single replaceable component of the bike and he wanted to show me all the work that had been done to it.

I ended up buying it that day, because it was a really good, fair price--and a steal for me. With all of the modifications done to it Yamaha could have charged $3,000, but instead they charged the fair market price, and it saved me a lot money in the long run. Plus, the bike had stupid low miles!

AND the original owner of the bike gave Yamaha all of the stock parts along with the bike. Now, Yamaha could have kept those parts and sold them separately, or charged me extra for them, but they didn't. They gave them to me along with the purchase.

The bike was ready for me the next day like they said it would be.

Another thing I appreciate about Rich is this: when he was working and talking with me a colleague came and asked him to reach out to another customer through phone but Rich refused to because he was working with me.

ALSO, I already had a pre-approved auto loan through my credit union and when I told Rich I had one, he stopped the financing process through Yamaha so that their credit checks wouldn't hurt my credit score--thank you. Honda screwed my wife's score bad with that. Rich didn't press on financing through Yamaha.

This store is dope. I'mma be back--with weapons (kidding). I'll be back for maintenance for my bike.< /Review>

<GmapID>0x80c2dca9ad3d9e31:0xed06a86dadb79117<//GmapID>< Text>
Trust. It's incredibly important for a motorcycle rider. Most of all trust between mechanic and rider. I can sum up our experience at Pasadena Yamaha with a few sew simple words...loyal customers from now on.

We spoke with Alex to begin with and he was so helpful with getting the bike off our truck and took his time talking to us about what the "issue" could be and etc. he was super nice and friendly. Some people have that warmth in their heart that you can just feel right off the bat. Well, the whole staff here was like that. The owner, Kal, is a patient and kind man. < time>
1584512597183<//time>
<rating>5</rating><Text>This place is a true gem. It's hidden within the windy roads of Portola Valley so only those who "know" and "care" would ever find this place. The restaurant is in a corner, sort of a steakhouse feel, but then with rustic yet somewhat modern finish. Fits the redwoods surrounding the village.

Let's start with the fresh baked bread that comes out. Oh my god, this is so good. No garnish needed. Just bread and butter. It already puts you in a fantastic mood and we had a tough time resisting to dig for more lest we fill our stomachs.

We tried the margherita pizza, linguine vongole, ceasar salad with anchovies, chicken tenders and spaghetti with fries. All the food is prepared "home-style". It definitely is not garnished and visually overdone. It stays truthful to the dish and you can definitely feel the chef's love. The chick tenders are freshly hand-made as one can tell by the irregular yet non congealed texture. The linguine was made with fresh clams, but again, staying truthful to the ingredients and bringing out its flavor. The pizza was simple, yet effective.

This is Californian / American high-end comfort food at its best. It does not get better than this - starting from the atmosphere all the way to desert. The staff is friendly and professional and the food is cooked with a degree of professional homeliness. Top all of this with not-too-bad prices. Again, not cheap. But very reasonable.

<Review>Whew, talk about overrated. It's not like this place is bad per se, but I don't know why anyone would eat here given all the other good restaurants in the Bay Area. Maybe if you live in Portola Valley, but otherwise it's definitely not worth going.

My wife made a reservation for us to go here with her parents visiting from outside the country. They really enjoy good food, and it was actually slightly embarrassing given how average the food was here.

Again, it's not like the food is awful or anything. But our standard for a good restaurant is that it should be better or more difficult than what we can cook at home. Food like roasted salmon, a hamburger, etc. don't count unless it's amazing, which here, it's just not.</Review>< pics>

<Rating>2< /Rating><Review>Staff friendly but food inconsistent. First time around, I ordered the Cajun wings which was a rub versus breaded and they were good, not spicy enough, but evenly cooked and crispy. I ordered them a second time and they were breaded with a sauce mixed in. The wings were not crispy or evenly cooked and it's possible they reused a crispy chicken wing order and just tossed in the sauce because of the taste. It was way different. They didn't taste fresh like the first time around. I also ordered some waffle fries that were super greasy and soggy. To top it off, some fries were still frozen. I live close enough but wasn't worth the trouble returning the order. If you do order from this place, check your food before leaving.<//Review>< Pictures>

<user_name>Reena Clions</user_name><response>None< /response>< time>
1571672488603</time>
<Rating>4</Rating><Review>I fell in love with Kokio in Cerritos and got myself hyped up finding out there is one closer to me in Harbor City!!
Then my excitement only left me with disappointment :/

CHICKEN:
- Half & Half ($20.50)
- Honey Bee: THIS IS THEIR SPECIALTY! Honestly with so many KFC (Korean Fried Chicken) shops around, this is what sets themselves apart. However, the flavor fell incredibly short to the Cerritos location - less crispy, less juicy, not as sweet.
- Hot Crispy: Original crispy but (barely) hot. This was super crispy but maybe too much flour/breading? It took me a couple bites to actually bite into the chicken.

SERVICE:
- There was only one server, which makes sense because it's more of a to-go shop. We were the only dine-in customers but he did a real good job serving us while taking care of phone/to-go orders
- Not sure what was going on but we started to hear loud yelling inside the kitchen (restaurant is quite small and we were sitting directly facing the kitchen). Seemed like the manager/owner was also involved but the yelling continued with cursing as well... it was to the point I was distracted in our conversations. This was a very uncomfortable experience at a small restaurant...

TIPS:
- Parking in the shared plaza (quite small and sketchy)
- No alcoholic drinks... which is usually a staple to KFC
- Maybe sit at the far ends (TV/kitchen can be distracting) or just order to-go

I know Kokio is good... this location is still new and need some improvements. So so sad to say but I would probably visit other OC locations in the meanwhile.<//Review><user_id>105794409513593571420</user_id>< Gmap_id>

< Review>
The salesman Chayse was very professional and we were able to pick the car up on the same day we test drove. I am disappointed that a vehicle like Land Rover does not have standard equipment like keyless entry like lower-end cars. I definitely would have chosen a different model if I had realized that. Yesterday, I started the vehicle and drove a distance and none of the console displays came on for Navigation, Media, Phone. First it only said ‚ÄúLand Rover‚Äù then went black altogether.  I feel there are some bugs to work out.

It does appear to be a solidly built vehicle with lots of safety features.

I was very un-thriller with their storage and cleaning accessory package that cost about $1000. Seemed like a waste if money.
